  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f67650d8-ea09-4d45-b855-403cf46b4cd4'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<a href="/questions/126723-hey-there-good-people-i-recently">Hey there good people!

I recently rented this book and the rest of its trilogy. But i couldn&#39;t find the first series anywhere i can afford. 
So, i guess i wouldn&#39;t be able to read the first series in the moment.

Can i start by reading this one?
And am i gonna enjoy and understand it or what?</a>
</div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/29114908-nevada"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/29114908-nevada">Nevada</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">While it has been a long time since I read the series, I remember the Legends series being a standalone from Chronicles. Chronicles will provide signi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">While it has been a long time since I read the series, I remember the Legends series being a standalone from Chronicles. Chronicles will provide significant backstory and greater depth of feeling for the characters, but you don't have wait. I also don't remember any spoilers in either.<br /><br />I loved these books (both series) and would hate for you to miss out because you were waiting for the others. Hope this helps!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_906612724" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906612724" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906612724?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780786918041" href="/book/show/774503.Time_of_the_Twins">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dungeons-and-dragons">dungeons-and-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=extraordinary-gentlemen">extraordinary-gentlemen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dragonlance">dragonlance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906612724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2154324554040502727"><i>"It is such a quiet thing, to fall. But far more terrible is to admit it.”</i><br/><br/>That line is unfortunately not from this book, nor even from this universe. However, in addition to being a favourite of mine, it describes this book perfectly.<br/><br/>The War of the Lance is over. The Queen of Darkness and her Dragon Highlords have been defeated against all odds. But Krynn is devastated by the conflict, and new dangers lurk in the shadows. In solitude in the Tower of High Sorcery, a familiar wizard is setting his</span>
  <span id="freeText2154324554040502727" style="display:none"><i>"It is such a quiet thing, to fall. But far more terrible is to admit it.”</i><br /><br />That line is unfortunately not from this book, nor even from this universe. However, in addition to being a favourite of mine, it describes this book perfectly.<br /><br />The War of the Lance is over. The Queen of Darkness and her Dragon Highlords have been defeated against all odds. But Krynn is devastated by the conflict, and new dangers lurk in the shadows. In solitude in the Tower of High Sorcery, a familiar wizard is setting his master plan into motion…<br /><br />With the beginning of the second trilogy of DragonLance novels, Margaret Weis and Tracy Hickman take the leap from classical, cliché-ridden, D&amp;D fantasy, to something much more interesting. <i>Time of the Twins</i> is the first real step on the path to this universe getting an identity of its own.<br /><br />In some ways, this is more of the same. In others, it’s a vast improvement. Characterisation has changed a lot. For the better. But the setting and storylines are similar to what we see in the first trilogy.<br /><br />Overall however, this is definitely my favourite DragonLance book so far. And look, it even has good writing!<br /><br /><i>"It is easy to have hope in the spring, warrior, when the weather is warm and the vallenwoods are green. It is easy to have hope in the summer, when the vallenwoods glitter with gold. It is easy to have hope in the fall when the vallenwoods are as red as living blood. But in the winter, when the air is sharp and bitter and the skies are gray, does the vallenwood die, warrior?"<br /><br />"Who spoke?" Caramon cried, staring around wildly, clutching his sword in his trembling hand.<br /><br />"What does the vallenwood do in the winter, warrior, when all is dark and even the ground is frozen? It digs deep, warrior. It sends its roots down, down, into the soil, down to the warm heart of the world. There, deep within, the vallenwood finds nourishment to help it survive the darkness and the cold, so that it may bloom again in the spring."<br /><br />"So?" Caramon asked suspiciously, backing up a step and looking around.<br /><br />"So you stand in the darkest winter of your life, warrior. And so you must dig deep to find the warmth and the strength that will help you survive the bitter cold and the terrible darkness. No longer do you have the bloom of spring or the vigor of summer. You must find the strength you need in your heart, in your soul. Then, like the vallenwoods, you will grow once more."</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2154324554040502727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_571331629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571331629" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571331629?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571331629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16673891651122199953">I feel kinda bad that it has taken me thirty years to finally get around to reading this second main Dragonlance trilogy. I mean, sure, it took me fifteen years to read the first Dragonlance trilogy and that was AFTER I had been playing D&D for years. Oops? Ah, but never mind that.<br/><br/>I discovered something awesome. This reads BETTER than the first trilogy. A lot more fun, more interesting, better characters (and not just Tolkien ripoffs), and a much more twisted story.<br/><br/>No, this isn't a classic fanta</span>
  <span id="freeText16673891651122199953" style="display:none">I feel kinda bad that it has taken me thirty years to finally get around to reading this second main Dragonlance trilogy. I mean, sure, it took me fifteen years to read the first Dragonlance trilogy and that was AFTER I had been playing D&amp;D for years. Oops? Ah, but never mind that.<br /><br />I discovered something awesome. This reads BETTER than the first trilogy. A lot more fun, more interesting, better characters (and not just Tolkien ripoffs), and a much more twisted story.<br /><br />No, this isn't a classic fantasy in most cases... but then... maybe it IS. Raistlin has that VIBE. Originally a dark hero master magician, like Elric from Moorcock's series, Raistlin is, in some ways, a lot more interesting, evil, and sympathetic than Elric. Awesomely powerful by the end of the original Trilogy, he's insufferably cocky and sure he could take over the world in a single day in this one. So he gets more ambitious. As in taking out the Dark Goddess to become a God, himself.<br /><br />In the meantime, his twin brother, a brawny, broken oaf of a warrior and pretty much Raistlin's opposite, has his own redemption arc going on because he let himself go to seed. Big time. And then we get a full corruption of a good cleric, time travel, Kinder mischief, and a big return to the awesomely big cataclysm from the Dragonlance's ancient past. And we get to see it from the ringside seats.<br /><br />Awesome? I think so.<br /><br />Let me be clear, however. I have only a little patience for money-grubbing franchises and the D&amp;D series as a whole definitely qualifies. I had some issues with the original trilogy, but somehow this book kinda pushes all my reservations aside. <br /><br />I had FUN. A lot of fun. And the writing is not bad at all. :) I can't wait to see the big, big events I've already been spoiled on by old friends back years ago. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16673891651122199953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_18713380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18713380" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18713380?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780394743516" href="/book/show/260039.Time_of_the_Twins">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18713380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11583955849874864816">I love this book despite the fact that about half of it is steeped in serious suckiness. The fact is, at least for me, that the excellent bits in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_' title='Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Time of the Twins</a> are far more excellent than the excellent bits in the three Dragonlance books that preceded this one (and those books had some excellent bits), making <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_' title='Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Time of the Twins</a> a favourite of mine.<br/><br/><b>Sucky Bits:</b><br/><u>Sucky --</u> This story hinges on the corruption of the Kingpriest of Istar. The Kingpriest arrogantly (and weakly) calls on the gods to com</span>
  <span id="freeText11583955849874864816" style="display:none">I love this book despite the fact that about half of it is steeped in serious suckiness. The fact is, at least for me, that the excellent bits in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a> are far more excellent than the excellent bits in the three Dragonlance books that preceded this one (and those books had some excellent bits), making <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a> a favourite of mine.<br /><br /><b>Sucky Bits:</b><br /><u>Sucky --</u> This story hinges on the corruption of the Kingpriest of Istar. The Kingpriest arrogantly (and weakly) calls on the gods to come down as peers and help him wipe evil from Krynn (the World of Dragonlance for the uninitiated). This is a solid idea for fantasy fiction, and it allows <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/869.Margaret_Weis" title="Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Margaret Weis</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/869.Margaret_Weis" title="Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Tracy Hickman</a> to express their idea about the need for equilibrium between good and evil. The problem is that we never see enough of the Kingpriest, his court, his "good/bad works" or anything else related to him to fully accept the Cataclysm he brings to Krynn. <br /><br />The authors rely on our Dragonlance-fed understanding of Krynn's history to fill in the Kingpriest-gaps rather than giving us the time we need in Istar to damn the Kingpriest ourselves. We know he's arrogant and foolish because we're told he is, not because they make us believe it. And that is sucky.<br /><br /><u>Suckier --</u> Something similar happens with the other important characters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a>. The gladiators, Kiiri and Pheragas, the priests, Quarath and Denubis, and the slavers, Raag and Arack, aren't given anywhere near the time they need to fulfill their potential as characters -- not even as supporting characters. Kiiri and Pheragas are supposed to be important to Caramon, but we're left to assume and accept their importance based on some barely developed camaraderie. Quarath, Arack and Raag are supposed to be the story's supporting villains, but they never movie beyond the Sneak, the pseudo-Mobster and the Muscle. Denubis (who returns later in the series) is the one true cleric left for Crysania to meet, and just as we are beginning to like him he disappears with an old, father-time style, Elven cleric. And all this is suckier. <br /><br /><u>Suckiest --</u> Tasslehoff Burrfoot. Tas is a favourite from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/259836.Dragons_of_Autumn_Twilight__Dragonlance_Chronicles___1_" title="Dragons of Autumn Twilight (Dragonlance Chronicles, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonlance Chronicles</a>. He is the lovable kender from who befriended a god and imbued the original stories with a sense of wonder. The authors lost their way with his character, though. He was designed to be a full-grown adult from a race cursed with insatiable curiousity and no fear. He is touched by the War of the Lance, and he learns how to fear for the lives of those he loves, which should make for a more mature character, a wiser more sober character. But Weis &amp; Hickman blow it. They turn Tas into a little boy. He feels like an insufferable, annoying, spoiled four year old. And that is the suckiest of all.<br /> <br /><b>Excellent Bits:</b><br /><u>Excellent --</u> All those sucky problems are offset by some cool stuff, though. One excellent element of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a> is Lady Crysania. She's second in commmand of the newly revived Order of Paladine -- cold, haughty, and utterly convinced of her natural superiority. But all that changes when she meets and is challenged by Raistlin, the dark wizard who has become the "Master of Past and Present." Her intellectual awakening at the hands of Raistlin is excellent.<br /><br /><u>Excellenter --</u> Caramon Majere, twin brother of Raislin, has his own struggle, but his is more a recovery than an awakening. He's a broken man when the story begins: broken by war, broken by being unnecessary when there's none left to kill, broken by his love for his brother. His story is the simplest, but also one of the most emotionally satisfying. Not a false note is struck in Caramon's rebirth, and there is even a promise of something more to come. This is even excellenter.<br /> <br /><u>Excellentest --</u> Nothing compares to the opening chapter in Raistlin's journey to become a god, however. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a> is Raistlin's tale, and when he's onstage the story is better than any other thing Weis &amp; Hickman have collaborated on. Raistlin does terrible things, it's true; he wears black robes (the mark of an evil wizard on Krynn), he murders people, he hungers for power, he manipulates and controls, he lies, and the god he wants to replace is Takhisis, the Queen of Darkness. He is a bad ass extraordinaire. But he also cares. He cares about dignity, he cares about the poor, he cares about the meek, he cares about his friends, he cares about his brother. He shows mercy, compassion and wisdom that no other character in all six of the core Dragonlance books possesses. He may be a badass, but he's also a hero, making him one of my all time favourite Fantasy characters. Raistlin's story is the excellentest part of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a>.<br /><br />The biggest problem with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonlance Legends</a>, then, and the main reason for the suckiness in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29187.Time_of_the_Twins__Dragonlance_Legends___1_" title="Time of the Twins (Dragonlance Legends, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of the Twins</a>, is that each installment of the three part series needed three parts to be fully realized. This series should have stretched over nine volumes, only then could it have achieved its full potential. But that's okay. I love it anyway. Even with all its flaws (yeah...I know...it's probably a nostalgia thing).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11583955849874864816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3429666976" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3429666976?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3429666976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11458493893988447938"><b>Actual rating is 4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>This is the first book of a trilogy. This takes place after the original trilogy and I suggest reading that trilogy first. In this one, it is two years after the events of the first trilogy. Raistlin is still all powerful and could achieve world domination but that isn't enough for him. Caramon is reeling from the fact that Raistlin chose the black robes. Meanwhile, a cleric of Paladine is convinced she could stop Raistlin and she seeks him out with help from Tasslehof</span>
  <span id="freeText11458493893988447938" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating is 4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />This is the first book of a trilogy. This takes place after the original trilogy and I suggest reading that trilogy first. In this one, it is two years after the events of the first trilogy. Raistlin is still all powerful and could achieve world domination but that isn't enough for him. Caramon is reeling from the fact that Raistlin chose the black robes. Meanwhile, a cleric of Paladine is convinced she could stop Raistlin and she seeks him out with help from Tasslehoff.<br /><br />What a terrific start to a new trilogy. We get some new, terrific character depth from these characters as well as time travel to Istar which was mentioned in the previous trilogy. What ties this book together is the theme of redemption. We have Crysannia who seeks redemption for Raistlin, Caramon who doesn't seek it but ends up on its path, and the Kingpriest who should be asking for it. I really like how it was tied in throughout. This could be my favorite setting in this universe as I love how it sets up that being narcissistic could lead to a downfall. And through out all these themes we have the contrast between the twins. Caramon loves his twin to a fault and Raistlin who is the "weaker" one supposedly but has become all powerful by evil ways.<br /><br />This is a reread for me and it still holds up. I know that a common complaint from the first trilogy that it was derivative. Even though one could argue the aspect of two brothers battling is nothing new this adds to that theme while bringing in some amazing concepts that will entertain all readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11458493893988447938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5412865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5412865" />
    <a title="Dale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/329383-dale"><img alt="Dale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448977473p2/329383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5412865?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dale" href="/user/show/329383-dale">Dale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/329383-dale?shelf=dragonlance">dragonlance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5412865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14984585014139010947">This was the first book I read when I started my new bus/train commute. But, this was not the first Dragonlance book I've ever read. It was the tenth. Dragonlance is a gigantic moneymaking franchise that runs off the insatiable appetites of geeks, among which I count myself. It's almost besides the point for me to review the book at all, because it's so niche. Either you "get it" or you don't. But, shoot, I'll give it a try.<br/><br/>The original Dragonlance trilogy (which I read in high school) was about</span>
  <span id="freeText14984585014139010947" style="display:none">This was the first book I read when I started my new bus/train commute. But, this was not the first Dragonlance book I've ever read. It was the tenth. Dragonlance is a gigantic moneymaking franchise that runs off the insatiable appetites of geeks, among which I count myself. It's almost besides the point for me to review the book at all, because it's so niche. Either you "get it" or you don't. But, shoot, I'll give it a try.<br /><br />The original Dragonlance trilogy (which I read in high school) was about a group of friends living in a fantasy world in which a medievalesque society exists alongside magic, gods, monsters, etc. The friends become unlikely heroes who play a central part in saving the world. Time of the Twins is the first book of a follow-on trilogy that focuses on the further adventures of two (and a half) of the original adventurers: twin brothers Caramon and Raistlin. These two characters will always have a soft spot in my heart. Big-hearted, simple-minded, strong and tough Caramon; frail, sickly, brilliant, manipulative Raistlin. Caramon is one of the world's greatest fighters, and Raistlin one of it's most potent wizards. They love each other and they hate each other. In every pair of brothers, or even friends, one is usually the Raistlin and one is the Caramon. I've been both.<br /><br />The "and a half" is the pint-sized thief Tasslehoff. He's a recurring character who is supposed to be comic relief, and he's hit or miss. Sometimes he's annoyng as crap, and sometimes he makes me laugh.<br /><br />But mostly the story is about Caramon and Raistlin, as they begin a new adventure. They end up going back in time, where Raistlin learns the secrets of a legendary wizard and Caramon becomes an infamous gladiator (and Tasslehoff causes general mischief), just before a Cataclysm is sent by the gods to punish a prideful humanity. And set the scene for book 2! Like I said, if you're a geek, this stuff is GREAT - all action and imagination. If that's not your cup of tea, it probably all seems silly and/or needlessly complicated. I eat this stuff up.<br /><br />There really is some good character development between the brothers, you just have to wade through a lot of genre tropes to get to it. But that characterization elevates the twins' story above your usual sword-n-sorcery hackwork. There's a general consensus among Dragonlance fans that "Legends" (as this trilogy about Caramon &amp; Raistlin is known) is the best among the literally hundreds of other Dragonlance volumes, and that's probably true.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14984585014139010947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2183654129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2183654129" />
    <a title="Joseph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5004971-joseph"><img alt="Joseph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523632271p2/5004971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2183654129?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph" href="/user/show/5004971-joseph">Joseph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11538366-time-of-the-twins">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183654129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3545194621431778068">It's actually kind of surprising that these books exist, at least in their current form.<br/><br/>The original Dragonlance Chronicles was the trilogy that launched a thousand other D&D tie-in novels; a wildly successful story in which the Forces of Evil were pitted against a half-elf, a dwarf, a <s>Hobbit</s>kender, a knight, a plainsman and a cleric. Oh, yes, and a fighter and his sickly twin brother mage. And there were epic journeys and dangers and setbacks, and a few tragic deaths, but in the end the aforeme</span>
  <span id="freeText3545194621431778068" style="display:none">It's actually kind of surprising that these books exist, at least in their current form.<br /><br />The original Dragonlance Chronicles was the trilogy that launched a thousand other D&amp;D tie-in novels; a wildly successful story in which the Forces of Evil were pitted against a half-elf, a dwarf, a <s>Hobbit</s>kender, a knight, a plainsman and a cleric. Oh, yes, and a fighter and his sickly twin brother mage. And there were epic journeys and dangers and setbacks, and a few tragic deaths, but in the end the aforementioned Forces of Evil were, in fact, defeated.<br /><br />And the follow-up trilogy took just about all of those elements and threw them right out the window, opting for a much more personal, much darker story.<br /><br />The time: A few years after the end of the War of the Lance. Although we begin with a reunion by all of the (surviving) heroes from the first trilogy, the focus shifts to a much smaller subset: the sickly mage Raistlin Majere, who, by the end of the first trilogy, had cast his lot with the powers of darkness even as he helped the others defeat the powers of evil; his twin brother Caramon; the cleric Crysiana, a new character who thinks she can redeem Raistlin (and also he makes her feel all fluttery, although she's not necessarily ready to admit that even to herself); and, of course, the irrepressible/irritating kender Tasslehoff Burrfoot, who continues in his role of kleptomaniac comic relief and occasional conscience.<br /><br />The years have not been kind to Caramon -- yes, he's now married to Tika, his sweetheart from the first trilogy, but he's also (not to put too fine a point on it) a fat drunkard driven to despair at the thought of his brother's fall from grace. But through circumstances he finds himself, together with Tasslehoff and Crysiana, traveling back through time to the city of Istar a thousand years past, in order to foil his brother's schemes.<br /><br />Remember Istar? The city that, in the original trilogy, is best known for getting smacked by the gods with a meteor or something because its Priestking got entirely too full of himself? Yes, that Istar. And time is growing short ...<br /><br />This is a difficult one to rate -- considered purely from a story perspective, it's much better &amp; more interesting than the original trilogy (which, to be sure, I enjoyed). But (as with the original trilogy) the actual prose is, um ... not great. To the point where there were times when if I'd had a red editor's pen, I would've been scribbling all over my Kindle. So it's just as well that I didn't have such a pen.<br /><br />And in the end I'm going with four stars because however painful I might find some of the sentences, I read the book in basically two or three sittings and will be moving immediately to the next in the trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3545194621431778068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15812761232900716893">I gave this book a 4, but I'm actually calling it a 4.5 because I absolutely devoured it. Fantasy books like this are my guilty pleasure, mainly because I feel like I should be spending my time reading "classics" and whatnot, but I had a blast diving back into the Dragonlance universe. I read some of the books when I was younger, and I'm ready to read some more!<br/><br/>I started with the Legends trilogy because, well... angsty brothers are my weakness. I remember loving Caramon and Raistlin and their co</span>
  <span id="freeText15812761232900716893" style="display:none">I gave this book a 4, but I'm actually calling it a 4.5 because I absolutely devoured it. Fantasy books like this are my guilty pleasure, mainly because I feel like I should be spending my time reading "classics" and whatnot, but I had a blast diving back into the Dragonlance universe. I read some of the books when I was younger, and I'm ready to read some more!<br /><br />I started with the Legends trilogy because, well... angsty brothers are my weakness. I remember loving Caramon and Raistlin and their complex relationship in the first Dragonlance books I read, and I still love them now.<br /><br />The subtraction of a half-star in my rating was because of Tasslehoff. The kender is, basically, everything I hate in a character, with his constant meddling and thievery and naivete. I just wanted him to sit still and stay out of the way, but alas.<br /><br />So... Yes, I loved this book, and I'm off to read the next!</span>

<div id="review_2957842305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2957842305" />

<span id="freeTextContainer9587668506550045682">Well... I first read this when I was 13. I must admit, when I opened it up on a whim and started reading it again three decades later, I expected to be partly amused, partly bemused. YA sprang to mind.<br/><br/>YA it might well be, but was I ever surprised. And I by that mean, I was REALLY surprised. A book hasn't captivated me like this in a long while. It drew me in as much as it did when I was a teenager, and time flew by... <br/><br/>This story brings everything to the table. Powerful descriptive prose; time tr</span>
  <span id="freeText9587668506550045682" style="display:none">Well... I first read this when I was 13. I must admit, when I opened it up on a whim and started reading it again three decades later, I expected to be partly amused, partly bemused. YA sprang to mind.<br /><br />YA it might well be, but was I ever surprised. And I by that mean, I was REALLY surprised. A book hasn't captivated me like this in a long while. It drew me in as much as it did when I was a teenager, and time flew by... <br /><br />This story brings everything to the table. Powerful descriptive prose; time travel; Cain and Abel revisited; a sincere questioning of the need for a balance between good and evil, and whether one can exist without the other. Even the Tasslehoff scenes had me laughing out loud (and I expected as a grumpy 'old' man to find him really, really annoying): they punctuated the serious psychological interplay between warrior hero Caramon, his dark mage twin Raistlin and the idealistic young priestess Crysania so well, in addition to being full of ironic humour (never let it be said our American cousins 'don't get' irony - they do, but use it more sparingly than we Brits).<br /><br />The storyline was mesmerising, the interaction of the major characters is so compelling you cannot help but be enthralled. Crysania was alienating in her self-righteous pomposity, and yet I could not turn away from her completely. How can you not feel for someone like that when they fall for a man like Raistlin, the would-be demon god of Krynn and the worlds beyond? And what sort of man is Raistlin, truly? Is he truly evil? Or just a progressive mage, streets ahead of 'old order' so-called good wizards like Par-Salian who seek to oppose him (at any cost)? What seems at first sight a simple good vs evil tale turns out to have a lot more nuance to it. Pretty impressive for 'YA'...<br /><br />Given that it was originally conceived (I believe) as a spin-off series based on a D&amp;D campaign brokered by RPG factory TSR in the 1980s, this book is nothing short of remarkable, and for me it has certainly weathered time; despite the odd obvious references from gaming ('spell components', 'continual light spells' etc) it didn't feel like a cheap rip-off but a genuine fantasy novel in its own right, one that engages the heart as much as it provokes thought. Hats off to Weiss and Hickman: I could say more, but I think you should just go out and get a copy for yourself.<br /><br />One final note: I don't even think this was a total nostalgia trip for me. Of course, some of that must inevitably have an impact on my opinion, but I certainly didn't approach it in that spirit: I fully expected to groan inwardly and silently chuckle at the 13-year-old me as I re-read it... I didn't. <br /><br />Revisiting this series has made me take a step back and ask myself if I shouldn't also revisit my own approach to writing fantasy. Both popular and textually rich, this is a fantastic piece of genre fiction anyone would be proud of writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9587668506550045682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1311596942?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7794113-joey-hines?shelf=dragonlance">dragonlance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13378576882317630544">I enjoyed the <i>Dragonlance Chronicles</i> in a Tolkien-lite type of way. <i>Time of the Twins</i>, however, really stands apart from the series that preceded it. This book mainly concerns the relationship between Caramon and Raistlin and the unpredictable force of Tasslehoff. These three were easily my favorite characters from <i>Chronicles</i>, so it's a thrill to see them get so much focus. New character Crysania has a well-developed struggle between her clerical faith and the callings of her heart, making this </span>
  <span id="freeText13378576882317630544" style="display:none">I enjoyed the <i>Dragonlance Chronicles</i> in a Tolkien-lite type of way. <i>Time of the Twins</i>, however, really stands apart from the series that preceded it. This book mainly concerns the relationship between Caramon and Raistlin and the unpredictable force of Tasslehoff. These three were easily my favorite characters from <i>Chronicles</i>, so it's a thrill to see them get so much focus. New character Crysania has a well-developed struggle between her clerical faith and the callings of her heart, making this a highly compelling read on a plot-and-character level.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book even more, though, for the philosophical questions it poses. The symbiotic relationship between the good, evil, and neutral forces of Krynn is explored in great depth, and the narration is fittingly ambiguous. By the end of the story, I was less sure than ever which characters were heroes or villains. And Caramon's love and loyalty for his (apparently) evil brother must be one of the most fascinating character traits in fantasy fiction.<br /><br />After reading <i>Time of the Twins</i>, I understand why Dragonlance gained the fanbase it did.<br /><br />"This is THE central theme of <i>Legends</i>: that we have no right to FORCE change on anyone. Change -- true change -- comes only from within. It is motivated, inspired, or invoked in others but never enforced. Faith is not dictated; it must come from within. Goodness and righteousness are not mandated; they must come from within. Every soul must choose for itself. This is the greatest gift of God. This simple lesson, if we could all learn it, would eliminate terrorism and warfare. It would revolutionize the world we know today. It can revolutionize our own personal worlds as well -- the world of our acquaintances, friends, and supposed enemies. It can change the world -- one soul at a time." - Tracy Raye Hickman</span>
  <a data-text-id="13378576882317630544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14750970781549202642">Like the Chronicles trilogy before it, this book is an oddly addictive hack job. Early on, you will find out Raistlin is thinly muscled. Then almost every chapter makes reference to his lean muscles. She felt his lean muscles through his robes. His thinly muscled form wrapped around her body. She could see his lean muscles through the silk of his black robes. Crysania also repeatedly smells his spell components while simultaneously noticing his thin muscles. These muscles can be found under his </span>
  <span id="freeText14750970781549202642" style="display:none">Like the Chronicles trilogy before it, this book is an oddly addictive hack job. Early on, you will find out Raistlin is thinly muscled. Then almost every chapter makes reference to his lean muscles. She felt his lean muscles through his robes. His thinly muscled form wrapped around her body. She could see his lean muscles through the silk of his black robes. Crysania also repeatedly smells his spell components while simultaneously noticing his thin muscles. These muscles can be found under his black robes, in case you forgot where they were and needed to double check whether they were lean or not.<br /><br />Caramon starts out fat, but later he gets hot again. (Spoilers if you're not good at foreseeing entirely predictable plotlines.) Too bad he has 80s hair.<br /><br />Anyway, this trilogy is more character-driven than anything that came before, and character is what the authors are worst at. So get ready for that. Some actions make no sense at all, and there are a couple direct contradictions.<br /><br />But I don't have the heart to give this less than three stars. Margaret and Tracy are my fantasy babies, and I love them. Plus, the last 30 pages were oddly compelling.</span>

<div id="review_762468280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/762468280" />
    <a title="Lindsay Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23929099-lindsay-scott"><img alt="Lindsay Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443693639p2/23929099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/762468280?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay Scott" href="/user/show/23929099-lindsay-scott">Lindsay Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23929099-lindsay-scott?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23929099-lindsay-scott?shelf=childhood-heroes">childhood-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23929099-lindsay-scott?shelf=books-i-will-always-reread">books-i-will-always-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762468280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17360277153444426729">RAISTLIN! Imagine my glee when I learned as an overexcitable preteen girl that there was a whole trilogy of books that featured my favorite character. (And apparently everyone else's.) Oh how my girlhood trembled. lol I wish I were kidding.<br/><br/>If I went back and read these books now, I'm sure I would still enjoy them despite the fact that I now see them in a different light. Sure, they aren't original and they use just about every fantasy cliche there is. But it's not like I knew that when I first r</span>
  <span id="freeText17360277153444426729" style="display:none">RAISTLIN! Imagine my glee when I learned as an overexcitable preteen girl that there was a whole trilogy of books that featured my favorite character. (And apparently everyone else's.) Oh how my girlhood trembled. lol I wish I were kidding.<br /><br />If I went back and read these books now, I'm sure I would still enjoy them despite the fact that I now see them in a different light. Sure, they aren't original and they use just about every fantasy cliche there is. But it's not like I knew that when I first read them. And so most likely, all I'd feel reading them now is a fond nostalgia. <br /><br />Come on, who can resist Raistlin? Hacking, frail, freaky-golden-eyed Raistlin? I certainly couldn't.<br /><br />*<br />8/4/18: I finally decided to reread a few of my Dragonlance books for the first time since I was a young teenager. I wanted to see if I still loved them as much as I did then. Unfortunately...they didn't really hold up. The nostalgia factor definitely improved things, but I think if I had come to these books as an adult, I would hate them. Of course, I suppose you have to keep in mind that every character plays to a D&amp;D alignment and that's why they're all kind of cookie cutter. But even so...the writing itself is just bad. Also, who was the editor for these? There were tons of grammatical errors, most often missing periods. <br /><br />Raistlin wasn't actually in this book much, but the scenes with him were much more underwhelming than I remember. He comes off a bit like an angsty teenager. (Uh oh...is that why he was my favorite character when I was a kid?) The only character that I honestly liked in this book was Tasslehoff. I know - he's the character everyone else hates. And he can be annoying at times, but he also keeps things more lighthearted and helps the book maintain a sense of wonder. So I appreciated his presence in this book. <br /><br />On to the next book in the trilogy, which I remember Raistlin being in a bit more. Maybe I'll remember why I liked him so much. <br /><br />Oh, and another thing I wanted to mention: there are two maps in this book. The first one shows Krynn in the present, and the second shows it 300 years in the past (the time they end up traveling to). It seems odd to me that the landscape could have changed so much in just 300 years. The spread of civilization, yes, okay, but the continent seems to have literally shifted and parts of it broken off. Doesn't that take longer...? I'm no scientist, though, so someone correct me if I'm wrong. Also, the 300-years-ago map was drawn by Tasslehoff, but how would he have known what the geography looked like? They spent all of their time in Istar. What was the point of even having that map? </span>
  <a data-text-id="17360277153444426729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1501332837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1501332837" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593734236p2/7206839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1501332837?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/7206839-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780880382656" href="/book/show/1254574.Time_Of_The_Twins">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1501332837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer572057546834583765">I'm glad I found a website that told me which order to read the Dragonlance books in. Of course, I thought to look it up after reading The Second Generation, which takes place after the Twins trilogy, but still. This first book in the trilogy is a fitting continuation of the Dragons trilogy. The Dragons of Spring Dawning ends in such a darkly suggestive way, and this book picks up on that tone right away. Weis and Hickman introduce new characters but bring back enough former characters to keep f</span>
  <span id="freeText572057546834583765" style="display:none">I'm glad I found a website that told me which order to read the Dragonlance books in. Of course, I thought to look it up after reading The Second Generation, which takes place after the Twins trilogy, but still. This first book in the trilogy is a fitting continuation of the Dragons trilogy. The Dragons of Spring Dawning ends in such a darkly suggestive way, and this book picks up on that tone right away. Weis and Hickman introduce new characters but bring back enough former characters to keep fans reading. They maintain their humor and their skill for suspense and moving a story along.<br />My only critique of this book is that it feels a little dragged out. From reading The Second Generation, I have an idea of what happens in this trilogy, and it seems like the plot could have been condensed. Not much REALLY happens in this book. At the same time, what does happen is well-paced and interesting enough to make me want to read the next book right away, which usually doesn't happen for me except in the cases of very suspenseful and/or very enjoyable reads. <br />I recommend this book to Dragonlance fans. If you're not a fan already, this book may get you there but may not. It definitely could stand on its own but also makes many references to earlier events and characters. I recommend reading Dragons first then reading these books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="572057546834583765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/408383804?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/7537497-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780786918041" href="/book/show/774503.Time_of_the_Twins">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer408383804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11613646607001113540"> I've been a Dragonlance fan since 1988. While I've loved most of the books, the Twins(Caramon and Raistlin Majere) were never my favorite characters. Friends have always said that Legends is a better trilogy than Chronicles (which started it all and am on my fourth reread.)<br/><br/> I probably should have listened to them. The first book was fantastic.<br/><br/> Raistlin(a powerful mage of the black robes(evil) and younger of the Twins)is one of the most devious characters around. He doesn't let you down, in his </span>
  <span id="freeText11613646607001113540" style="display:none"> I've been a Dragonlance fan since 1988. While I've loved most of the books, the Twins(Caramon and Raistlin Majere) were never my favorite characters. Friends have always said that Legends is a better trilogy than Chronicles (which started it all and am on my fourth reread.)<br /><br /> I probably should have listened to them. The first book was fantastic.<br /><br /> Raistlin(a powerful mage of the black robes(evil) and younger of the Twins)is one of the most devious characters around. He doesn't let you down, in his quest for greater power that others cannot begin to comprehend. <br /> Caramon (fighter and self-appointed protector of his brother) is basically what you see is what you get has started his path back to the light after losing his way two years after the War of the Lance(Chronicles) has ended. <br /> Their connection is an odd one. Best summed up by their friend Tanis:" I would trust Caramon with the groups' lives but he would spill our blood on Raistlin's word in a heartbeat." <br /><br />Dragonlance itself is a 'LotR lite.'They are quick reads. Unlike Tolkien's work, however, it's a larger body of work consisting of more books. So the rich history is there to enjoy. <br /><br />On to reading book two. No spoilers but if anybody has questions-feel free to ask.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11613646607001113540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48599723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48599723" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1924971-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442502236p2/1924971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48599723?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/1924971-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1924971-david?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48599723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16432550919858242562">This is a fabulous tale and if you want to read any Dragonlance series, this is it. It’s a tale involving going back in time which is normally fraught with difficulty in writing a sensible plot. The authors’ do this amazingly well and this is a haunting tale. Characterisation is brilliant and fantasy fans will be enthralled by the main characters. Cameron and Raistlin are twins but more different twins you could not get. In this tale Cameron is a shadow of his former strength. Drink has brought </span>
  <span id="freeText16432550919858242562" style="display:none">This is a fabulous tale and if you want to read any Dragonlance series, this is it. It’s a tale involving going back in time which is normally fraught with difficulty in writing a sensible plot. The authors’ do this amazingly well and this is a haunting tale. Characterisation is brilliant and fantasy fans will be enthralled by the main characters. Cameron and Raistlin are twins but more different twins you could not get. In this tale Cameron is a shadow of his former strength. Drink has brought him to a sorry state and not even his kinder friend, Tas, can help. Into the tale comes Crysania and she believes strongly in Paladin. She is persuaded on a quest by Raistlin who clearly has his own agenda. In his haste for power he has been cursed and he sees the world through hour glass eyes and everything decays as he watches. Raistlin wants to challenge the Dark Queen, but to do so he must travel back in time to destroy Fistandalus, the worlds greatest ever sorcerer. This is cleverly written and surprisingly believable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16432550919858242562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1371797396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1371797396" />
    <a title="Zoran Krušvar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1157189-zoran-kru-var"><img alt="Zoran Krušvar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442502974p2/1157189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371797396?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoran Krušvar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoran Krušvar" href="/user/show/1157189-zoran-kru-var">Zoran Krušvar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371797396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12785082238829834440">"Dragonlance: Legends" is actually a good series. And that's weird, because game-inspired books do tend to suck big time. I give most credit for complexity of Raistlin's character and for the fact that Caramon suffers from PTSD. And that's just great, because too often fantasy heroes tend to be completely immune to distress and we know that human mind doesn't work that way. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_432648666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/432648666" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/432648666?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dru" href="/user/show/8273355-dru">Dru</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780880382656" href="/book/show/1254574.Time_Of_The_Twins">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8273355-dru?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8273355-dru?shelf=gaming">gaming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer432648666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2176903309794249732">This second trilogy of the original Dragonlance novels doesn't *quite* hold up to the first trilogy. As we are no longer in a story about a "party of adventurers", it has lost a bit of its D&D flavor. Gone are most magic or cleric spells. Characters *rarely* use magic. And it's mostly about how stupid Caramon is with regard to his brother. All in all, I'm dropping this from 4 to 3 stars.<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>Below is my old review of the book<br/>-------------------------------<br/>This will be my same review for all 7 books i</span>
  <span id="freeText2176903309794249732" style="display:none">This second trilogy of the original Dragonlance novels doesn't *quite* hold up to the first trilogy. As we are no longer in a story about a "party of adventurers", it has lost a bit of its D&amp;D flavor. Gone are most magic or cleric spells. Characters *rarely* use magic. And it's mostly about how stupid Caramon is with regard to his brother. All in all, I'm dropping this from 4 to 3 stars.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Below is my old review of the book<br />-------------------------------<br />This will be my same review for all 7 books in the original double-trilogy (plus the 7th add on years later).<br /><br /><br /><br />There are few D&amp;D novelizations out there that are really worth reading. Only two series have I loved, and the original 6 (became 7) "Dragonlance" novels are one of those great series. (Gord the Rogue is the other).<br /><br />At first when I read this, I was a bit put off because the "Krynn" world did not "agree" with D&amp;D. The gods had different names (Bahamut = Paladine, Tiamut = Takhesis) and the race of Halflings were known as "Kender". But getting past these small issues, the story eventually became *exactly* what a good D&amp;D story should be -- a *PARTY* of mixed races and classes, each with their own strengths and weaknesses, on an adventure where each party member has a time to shine. This is gaming-turned-novel at its best.<br /><br />All in all, the world was large and diverse and engaging. There was adventure, love stories, human frailty, power struggles, etc. I eventually played a Necromancer in D&amp;D and patterned a number of his character traits (physical frailty, lust for power) after Raistlin. That was my way of showing how much I loved these novels.<br /><br />I gave some of the other "Dragonlance" novels a shot, but quickly lost interest. They just didn't have the draw that the original series did.<br /><br />Read them and enjoy.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9771491591259012237">I don't know where to begin with this book. I know that I'm going to love this series just as much as The Chronicle Trilogy. I have become so wrapped up with these books, that I’m actually bugging my friends who have read these back when they first came out, to re-read the series so we can discuss them.   <span id="freeText9771491591259012237" style="display:none">I don't know where to begin with this book. I know that I'm going to love this series just as much as The Chronicle Trilogy. I have become so wrapped up with these books, that I’m actually bugging my friends who have read these back when they first came out, to re-read the series so we can discuss them. Yes, I am a Dragonlance virgin! <br /> <br />I can’t believe that Camaron has changed so much in two years. If I was Tika, I would have slapped some sense into him with a heavy frying pan. I was so hurt to see how he changed and treated her. I love how Tas stepped up to make sure that Camaron followed through with Tika’s orders. I’m a little confused about Crysania and Raistlin. I realize that she is falling in love with him, but with that love, she also exhibits hate. I hope that this love doesn’t prove to be what the story is leading it to be. As for my beloved Tas, he is just so under appreciated by everyone. Then there is Raistlin. Well, who can trust a man with hour glass shaped pupils and golden skin. I have high hopes for Raist, but then he always turns and becomes the evil and untrusting person that he is.<br /><br />I’ve become so obsessed with these books that I have a hard time focusing on other books that I need to review. I’m so excited about starting the next installment, War of the Twins. Again, I want to thank my friends Mike and Aj for turning me onto this addicting story! <br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14628981542573286795"><i>Dragons of Autumn Twilight</i> was amazing, and somehow this book managed to be even better!<br/>I loved the dialogues and the refined, archaic-ish writing style, I find it perfect for the epic fantasy genre. The little cameos and the humorous parts were also really enjoyable. The plot was even more interesting than that of <i>Dragons of Autumn Twilight</i>, I guess mostly because it involved less main characters rather than a whole bunch of them, including some I personally never grew to care about. This time,</span>
  <span id="freeText14628981542573286795" style="display:none"><i>Dragons of Autumn Twilight</i> was amazing, and somehow this book managed to be even better!<br />I loved the dialogues and the refined, archaic-ish writing style, I find it perfect for the epic fantasy genre. The little cameos and the humorous parts were also really enjoyable. The plot was even more interesting than that of <i>Dragons of Autumn Twilight</i>, I guess mostly because it involved less main characters rather than a whole bunch of them, including some I personally never grew to care about. This time, the main characters involved were fewer and already dear to me and thus, more enjoyable to read about. <br />Another thing I also loved was the way the authors presented and described the character development (if you can call it that) of Lady Crysania. The way she went from a Priestess completely devoted to her faith and to the Light.... to a comfused person who questions her beliefs and realizes there are faults in them after all.... and finally, to a person who changes her mind and decides to embrace the Darkness in hopes of finding the answers she searches for there. <br />Same goes for Caramon's character development, which is of a different type, but equally good.<br />P.S. Raistlin's manipulation skills are A+ XD<br />The last chapters in particular had me at the edge of my seat! All in all, a stunning book. Hope the next one is equally good!</span>

<div id="review_1550409713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1550409713" />
    <a title="Bianca Klein Haneveld" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18736207-bianca-klein-haneveld"><img alt="Bianca Klein Haneveld" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428072217p2/18736207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1550409713?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bianca Klein Haneveld" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bianca Klein Haneveld" href="/user/show/18736207-bianca-klein-haneveld">Bianca Klein Haneveld</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1550409713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17586249479057975305">Since this book stands out for the way it offers insights in its very interesting characters, I will focus this review on them.<br/>The titular twins Caramon and Raistlin stole my heart in the original trilogy. Caramon, brave, good, honest and completely devoted to his twin brother. Raistlin, bitter, brilliant, evil on first sight but oddly (but convincingly) compessionate at key moments... they are fascinating. This book hints at ways to see their complex relationship that makes these characters eve</span>
  <span id="freeText17586249479057975305" style="display:none">Since this book stands out for the way it offers insights in its very interesting characters, I will focus this review on them.<br />The titular twins Caramon and Raistlin stole my heart in the original trilogy. Caramon, brave, good, honest and completely devoted to his twin brother. Raistlin, bitter, brilliant, evil on first sight but oddly (but convincingly) compessionate at key moments... they are fascinating. This book hints at ways to see their complex relationship that makes these characters even more wellrounded.<br />Added to that mix is an interesting lady Crysiana. She is captivating. Self-righteous, cold to people who don't know her, with a fatal vanity... but oh so tender, kind, intelligent and vulnerable once someone scratches the surface. Unfortunately - Raistlin is the first one who does ;-).<br />This book is imaginative and feels like a welcome return to the Dragonlance-world.<br /><br />Some assides though: the plot hinges on Raistlin remaining a mystery for the most part. You get to know many of his actions and some of his intentions - but I would have loved to see the world through his eyes and missed this.<br />And another reviewer (Brad) explains expertly how Tasslehoff Burrfoot is somewhat short-changed in this trilogy. In short: this lovable kender who learned to fear by berievement and handled it admirably, is an almost childish comic relief here. Which made me sad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17586249479057975305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8954967481480053567" style="display:none">You know what? I'm on a review hiatus but I feel compelled to write a review just for this book. It is 4:33 am and I need to review this specific book. <br /><br />Time of the Twins has a way of outshining its dependence on tropes and corny dialogue. I don't know how it happened, but this book somehow transcends itself in a way that is nothing short of enchanting. You love it like you love an easy chair after a long day or a favorite episode you've seen a thousand times. Sometimes you realize what's happening is tremendously tropey and overcooked but you find yourself enjoying it anyway--that's how good this book is. At times, it is straight-up spiritual. <br /><br />Also Raistlin is bae.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hwpYgJEZ5N3XLPTzhWRM/0I3gquvSweuFQ7aHVwZAavf191wHGncVQHOd+4zYTkz6PYTzcVFqgASje9lyuhtBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FRzbnd6no3kklI9OAv2U21GUChKypil89bwQto/TQyVNwV5tU9eb8fJ2DFO0+OEX+1WbdNiohNLyPyXOGSIviA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11647116613716793574">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two para</span>
  <span id="freeText11647116613716793574" style="display:none">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two paranormal romance novels, Fallen Angel and Warrior Angel, with my daughter, Elizabeth Baldwin. I graduated from the University of Missouri–Columbia and now live in Wisconsin with dogs, Max, Dixie, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am currently working on the third book in the Dragon Brigade series, the Seventh Sigil. The first book is Shadow Raiders. The second book is Storm Riders, coming out from Tor in July 2013. <br /><br />My hobby is flyball racing with my dogs, Dixie, a border collie, and two crackhead Shelties, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am the owner of the company, Margaret Weis Productions, publisher of RPGs. Our newest project is creating the RPG for the wonderful TV series, Firefly. Shiny!</span>

Let me make this as plain as I know how." Now it was his turn to stand up. Pressing his thin hands upon the desk, he leaned towards her, like a snake.<br />"I don't give damn about the world!" he said softly. "I could rule it tomorrow, if I wanted it! I don't.&rdquo;</span>
